Louis Christo’¼Ćersen (s102928)
==PAGE:78==
3.2.
3D Growth-method
60
when growing structures using beam elements is the occasional addition of a ŌĆØlonelyŌĆØ new node. By
lonely is meant a new node which does not get any new members connected to it. It can be hard to see
from the ’¼ügures above, but from iteration 23 to 24 (Figure 3.26k to Figure 3.26l) and from iteration
24 to 25 (Figure 3.26l to Figure 3.26m) two of these lonely nodes are introduced in the top tension
member. Such a lonely node would make a truss structure unstable, but due to the bending sti’¼Ćness
of the beam elements introducing a lonely node can in some cases decrease the total volume of the
structure. In this example the initial volume is reduced by 28.3 % and the run-time is 100 minutes (4
cores).
E’¼Ćect of compliance constraint and bending
So far in the 3D growth-method a compliance constraint of 1.0 times the initial compliance has been
used. In this section the e’¼Ćect of varying this constraint will be studied for the beam element tripod
cantilever. Loosening the constraint, i.e. setting it equal to for example two or three times the initial
compliance, is expected to reduce the number of lonely nodes added during the optimization. The
lonely nodes are added when the bending (EI) starts to dominate the axial forces (EA), which happens
when the ratio of element length divided by the radius of its cross-section goes down. Loosening the
compliance constraint should allow the optimizer to keep this ratio relatively large and therefore fewer
lonely nodes should be observed.
In Figure 3.27 below a 50 iteration optimization of the tripod
cantilever using beam elements and compliance constraints of 1, 2, and 3 times the initial compliance
can be seen.
First, it is noticed that increasing the compliance constraint to 2 or 3 times the initial compliance pro-
duces an optimized structure containing signi’¼ücantly more elements added in the expected systematic
manner. This indicates that less lonely nodes are added in these two structures. In Figure 3.28 below
a zoom of the optimized structure with a compliance constraint of 1 times the initial compliance (see
Figure 3.27a) is shown.
The purple rings indicate clusters of lonely nodes, which are not found in the other two optimized
structures (Figures 3.27b and 3.27c). This seems to con’¼ürm the anticipated e’¼Ćect of loosening the
compliance constraint. Last, the ratio of element length to element radius is investigated. This ratio
was expected to increase as the compliance constraint was loosened. The mean value of this ratio
is calculated for each of the three optimized structures to 8.89, 26.51, and 47.03 for Figures 3.27a,
3.27b, and 3.27c respectively. Again the anticipated result is obtained. It can be concluded that
the magnitude of the compliance constraint plays a signi’¼ücant role in determining how the optimizer
grows the structure. Loosening the constraint results in less lonely nodes by increasing the ratio of
element length to element radius and produces optimized structures that follow the expected system-
atic growth instead of introducing lonely nodes.
Another way to reach the same conclusion as the one above is to study the bending stresses and the
axial stresses. The bending stresses which are associated with the sti’¼Ćness EI should, if the same
conclusion is to be reached, be signi’¼ücantly smaller in magnitude than the axial stresses which are
associated with the sti’¼Ćness EA. Furthermore it should be found that the axial stresses attain the
same value for each element in the structure, as the speci’¼üc formulation of the optimization problem
used in this work should produce a uniformly stressed design. The bending stresses are calculated
using NavierŌĆÖs formula:
Žā = Mr
I
(3.5)
where M is the moment, r is the radius of the cross-section, and I is the moment of inertia. For
the three optimized structures shown in Figures 3.27a, 3.27b, and 3.27c the maximum bending stress

(looking at both bending in the y-direction and in the z-direction) divided by the normal stress is
found to 2.630, 2.547, and 0.063 respectively. It is seen that the ratio gets lower as the compliance
constraint is loosened, which emphasizes that bending becomes less important for looser compliance
constraints. As bending becomes less and less important the structure acts more and more like a truss
structure instead of a frame structure.
The axial stress is found to ŽāEA = 1.855, ŽāEA = 7.326, and ŽāEA = 16.515, respectively. The axial

6 supports can be seen.

A total of 69 nodes has been added, and as expected the ball-like shape is more detailed and clear
than when only using 4 supports. The optimizer has more supported nodes from which it can add the
red compression strings, and therefore this structure can represent a perfect sphere better than the
one with only 4 support nodes. The initial volume is reduced by 97.3 % and the run-time is recorded
to 4223 minutes (12 cores).
It has been attempted, without success, to create optimized structures with more than 6 support/load
nodes. The growth-method does not perform well when there are a lot of members in the initial
structure. Due to its systematic way of growing the structure it performs much better on a simple
initial structure with few members. This is also why no distributed load case examples are studied in
this thesis, as initial structures subjected to distributed load would consist of numerous members.

First it is observed that the total volume (Vtotal) increases as the constraint gets stricter. This trend
makes sense as it becomes more and more expensive to use the circular part of the design domain.
In order to comply with the compliance constraint and the increasingly stricter geometric constraint
the optimizer has to increase the total volume. It is also noticed that the violating volume (Vviolation)
decreases as the constraint gets stricter.
This trend veri’¼ües the whole purpose of the geometric
constraint, i.e. to move volume outside of the circle. Notice that with pfac = 11.0 the structure
does not violate the constraint at all, as mentioned earlier. As for the real volume (Vreal) a speci’¼üc
trend is not observed. This is due to the fact that the optimizer can reduce the objective function by
either lowering Vviolation or Vreal. To illustrate this a plot of Vtotal, Vreal, and Vviolation as a function
of iterations for pfac = 2.5 is shown in Figure 3.39 below.
Figure 3.39: Volumes as a function of iterations (pfac = 2.5).
The plot shows how the real volume and the violating volume are not constantly decreasing. They
generally decrease with every iteration, but for some iterations they can also increase. However the
combined e’¼Ćect of the two volumes causes the total volume to decrease with every iteration.
Louis Christo’¼Ćersen (s102928)
==PAGE:87==
Chapter 4
Conclusion
This chapter contains the ’¼ünal conclusion of the work related to this masterŌĆÖs thesis. Suggestions for
further work will be given at the end of this chapter.
4.1
Summary and Conclusion
In two dimensions the growth-method developed throughout this master thesis has shown ability to
reproduce analytical solutions. First a short cantilever with an unbounded bounding box was op-
timized. The optimal structureŌĆÖs resemblance to the ŌĆØMichell-cantileverŌĆØ is uncanny and when its
volume is compared to that of the ŌĆØMichell-cantileverŌĆØ a deviation of only 0.079 % was found. A
longer cantilever (h by 3.35889h) with a tight bounding box was also optimized by the growth-method
in order to compare its optimal volume with that of an equivalent ŌĆØMichell-structureŌĆØ. For this ex-
ample the results also compare very well with a deviation of merely 0.055 %. The growth-method is
tested on other structures than ŌĆØMichell-structuresŌĆØ, such as a crane structure, a structure with two
loads (the butter’¼éy), a structure utilizing a vast amount of supports, and several multiple load case
structures. For the crane structure and the butter’¼éy example the growth-method produces simple
solutions by growing the structures in a systematic manner. The volume (the objective function)
is decreased in every growth and the solutions take on a natural and simplistic form. The circular
supported cantilever demonstrates the methodŌĆÖs ability to utilize boundary nodes when needed. If
the initial structure is provided with many boundary nodes the optimizer will make use of them when
appropriate and it was shown that the volume could be reduced even further for this example than
for a simple cantilever (with only two supports) with similar dimensions.
The multiple load case
examples showcase one of the major di’¼Ćerences between the growth-method developed in this master
thesis and the one presented in [10]. Due to the simultaneous topology and shape optimization uti-
lized in this work it is possible to optimize multiple load case examples. A cantilever, a beam, and a
frame is optimized with multiple load cases and the growth-method again builds up the structure in
a systematic way while reducing the volume in every growth. Despite its ability to optimize multiple
load case examples, there is one de’¼ünite drawback using the growth-method in this work compared
to the one presented in [10]. The run-time is signi’¼ücantly longer in this Matlab-based method than
in the program TTO from http://www.upct.es/ deyc/software/tto.php which is written in c++ and
developed as a result of the work presented in [10].
The extension of the growth-method to three-dimensional structures is a ’¼ürst attempt in this thesis,
as no other works describing the growth-method in 3D has been found. The method works in exactly
the same way, although stability issues has to be dealt with. The issues are handled by eigenvalue
constraints or beam elements. Both ways are tested on a simple 3D tripod cantilever and the beam
element solutions is found to be much simpler and easier to interpret. For the 3D growth-method
69
==PAGE:88==
4.2.
Suggestions for further work
70
it is attempted to obtain the classical Michell torsion-ball solution to a cantilever subjected to pure
torsion. The spherical structure is obtained nicely by the growth-method optimizer and resembles
the classical solution. However it was not possible to compare the optimal volume to the analytical
volume as for the 2D cantilever structures. This is due to the fact that beam elements were used,
and even though the bending stresses are lower than the axial stresses in the optimal structure they
are not negligible and therefore the volume is not comparable to the analytical one which is based
on truss elements. A multiple load case example is also studied for the 3D method. A simple crane
structure with a vertical and a horizontal load case is analyzed and the initial volume is reduced by
38.9 %. As proven by the very long run-time the growth-method struggles to ’¼ünd optimal solutions
for 3D multiple load case examples. A drawback with the 3D growth-method is that the utilization
of beam elements often results in non-neglegible bending stresses and therefore a truss structure is
not obtained. An investigation of the compliance constraint shows though, that for some structures
it is possible to obtain dominant axial stresses (truss-like behaviour) by loosening the compliance
constraint. Furthermore the growth-method struggles, especially in 3D, when the initial structure is
complicated and consists of many members. This is why examples including distributed load has not
been presented.
As for the practical applications of the growth-method many of the examples presented in this master
thesis are probably too complicated to construct e’¼āciently in real life. To provide more practical
application assets to the growth-method a geometric constraint has been implemented. This constraint
is a circular constraint which can be used to make room for e.g. ventilation. The growth-methodŌĆÖs
ability to produce Michell structures can be of architectural interest. As mentioned in [3] the optimal
Michell structures are of great interest at one of the largest and most in’¼éuential engineering ’¼ürms
Skidmore, Owings & Merrill.
4.2
Suggestions for further work
The most crucial topic for further work is in the authorŌĆÖs opinion run-time. The run-time of the
current Matlab-based growth-method is relatively long when compared to the program on which it is
based, TTO. Several measures has been taken in order to improve the run-time, but it still does not
quite compare to the TTO program.
Another interesting feature to look further into is the geometric constraints. Applying these in other
shapes, such as rectangles or triangles, and most importantly to implement them in three-dimensional
structures would be of great interest. This would allow for optimization of more realistic structures.
Last, it would be useful to work on a way to reduce the bending stresses for the 3D beam element
model and make them negligeble compared to the axial stresses. This might not be possible for all
kinds of structures, which is why a completely di’¼Ćerent method of maintaining stability also might be
interesting to look at.
Louis Christo’¼Ćersen (s102928)

Appendix A
Shortest distance between 3D-segments
Consider two lines in the three-dimensional space given by
L1 :
P(s) = P0 + s (P1 ŌłÆP0) = P0 + su
(A.1)
L2 :
Q(t) = Q0 + t (Q1 ŌłÆQ0) = Q0 + tv
(A.2)
where s and t ranges from negative in’¼ünity to positive in’¼ünity, P0 and P1 are any two points on L1,
and Q0 and Q1 are any two points on L2. A vector between points on the two lines can be de’¼üned as
w(s, t) = P(s)ŌłÆQ(t). The shortest distance between the two lines will therefore occur at the location
(sC, tC) for which w (sC, tC) is the unique minimum for w(s, t). The shortest distance is called wC
and is illustrated in Figure A.1 below.
Figure A.1: Shortest distance (wC) between two lines in 3D (Taken from [19]).
It can be shown mathematically (derivation is beyond the scope of this thesis) that the location (sC, tC)
can be found by
sC = be ŌłÆcd
ac ŌłÆb2
and
tC = ae ŌłÆbd
ac ŌłÆb2
(A.3)
where a = u ┬Ę u, b = u ┬Ę v, c = v ┬Ę v, d = u ┬Ę w0, e = v ┬Ę w0, and w0 = P0 ŌłÆQ0. With the location
known the shortest distance between the two lines can be found as
1
==PAGE:98==
APPENDIX A. SHORTEST DISTANCE BETWEEN 3D-SEGMENTS
d(L1, L2) = |P(sC) ŌłÆQ(tC)|
(A.4)
It is extremely important to notice that this shortest distance might not be located within the bound-
aries of the elements e1 and e2. Elements are ’¼ünite and they should therefore be considered as segments
rather than in’¼ünite lines. The two lines in Equations (A.1) and (A.2) can easily be reformulated as
segments or elements simply by letting 0 Ōēżs Ōēż1 and 0 Ōēżt Ōēż1, P0 and Q0 be the start points
of the elements, and P1 and Q1 be the end points of the elements. The ’¼ürst step in computing the
shortest distance for segments is to calculate the shortest distance wC for the in’¼ünite lines on which
the segments lie on. If the location (sC, tC) is in the range of the respective segments then the cal-
culated distance wC is also the shortest distance for the segments. If this is not the case, it can be
proven mathematically (derivation is beyond the scope of this thesis) that the shortest distance will
be located on the boundary of a subregion H of the (s, t)-plane de’¼üned by
H = {(s, t)|0 Ōēżs Ōēż1
and
0 Ōēżt Ōēż1} = [0, 1] ├Ś [0, 1]
(A.5)
All four edges given by s = 0, s = 1, t = 0, and t = 1 have to be checked in order to ’¼ügure out where
on the boundary of H the shortest distance occurs. It can be shown (derivation is beyond the scope
of this thesis) that the shortest distance along for example the edge s = 0 occurs at (0, t0) where:
t0 = v ┬Ę w0
v ┬Ę v
(A.6)
The other edges are treated in a similar manner and the one producing the shortest distance is found.

Appendix E
ipOPT vs. fmincon
In this section a very brief comparison of the two optimizers ipOPT and fmincon is performed. The
comparison is based on the short cantilever example in 2D, which is run for 5 iterations using both
optimizers. In Figure E.1 on the next page the left column shows the optimized structures using
ipOPT and the right column is for fmincon.
First it is noticed that the ’¼üfth iteration is the same for both optimizers, only mirrored. Second it can
be seen that the path taken by the two optimizers to the ’¼ünal optimized structure is quite di’¼Ćerent.
The initial volume is reduced by exactly 25.2 % in both cases. Both optimizers perform equally well
in minimizing the objective function, but when looking at run-times ipOPT uses 217 seconds whereas
fmincon uses only 26 seconds. When using ipOPT a lot of di’¼Ćerent parameters can be set by the
user, and these may a’¼Ćect the run-time to a certain extent. This brief comparison can therefore not
conclude that fmincon is always better. No con’¼ügurations of the parameters in ipOPT which reduce
the run-time further has been found, and it is therefore decided to use fmincon in this thesis.
11

APPENDIX F. THE BUTTERFLY
The growth algorithm again systematically builds up the structure, except for a few times where the
routine is broken (see Figures F.2j and F.2o). The ’¼ünal structure ends up being perfectly symmetric
though, as expected due to the two loads being symmetric, with the same number of tension and
compression chords. In this example the initial volume is reduced by 61.4 % and the run-time was
recorded to 796 minutes (12 cores). In Figure F.3 below the normalized volume and run-time is plotted
as a function of added nodes.
Figure F.3: Normalized volume and run-time as a function of new nodes added.
The sum of two exponential functions (see Equation (3.1)) is again found to serve as the best ’¼üt to
the decrease in volume. The ’¼üt is made on nodes 10-80 to give a more accurate representation of the
decrease in volume for n > 80. The constants are found to a = 0.0273, b = ŌłÆ0.0925, c = 0.3884, and
d = ŌłÆ6.862 ┬Ę 10ŌłÆ5.

Appendix G
Multiple load cases - frame with wind
loading
This example demonstrating the performance of the growth-method in two dimensions is a simple
frame with two load cases. The example is supposed to resemble a frame subjected to wind-load. The
two load cases are constructed so that the wind-load is allowed to come from both directions. The
initial structure with applied boundary conditions and the two load cases can be seen in Figure G.1
below. Bounding box is de’¼üned by the dotted red line.
Figure G.1: Boundary and load conditions for the two load cases example (frame).
A total of 17 iterations is run for this example. The initial optimized structure (topology only) along
with selected optimized structures can be seen in Figure G.2.

TopOpt.m
% Topology optimization program
% Modified 14/03ŌłÆ2014 by MJB
% Modified 24/08ŌłÆ2015 by LMC
clc; clear all; close all; format shortg
addpath('Input')
% Loading input file
testfile
% testfile2
% Cantilever
% Lbeam
% Chose to plot structure during optimization (1 = yes, 2 = no)
Popt = 2;
% Objective compliance (1) or volume (2)
Opt = 2;
% Additional options
lwmax = 8;
% Maximum line width for plots
Amin = 1eŌłÆ6;
% Minimum area per element (TopOpt)
Amax = 10;
% Maximum area per element (TopOpt)
VCon = 1;
% Percent change of initial volume when constrained
CCon = 1;
% Percent change of initial compliance when constrained
% Initializing
ne = size(IX,1);
% Number of elements
% Saving input in data
data.X=X;data.IX=IX;data.mprop=mprop;data.loads=loads;data.bound=bound;
data.Popt=Popt;data.lwmax=lwmax;IXorg = IX;
% Vector of element areas
Ar0 = zeros(ne,1);
for e = 1:ne
Ar0(e) = mprop(IX(e,3),2);
end

H.1. TOPOPT.M
APPENDIX H. CODE
data.Ar = Ar0;
% Constrain on total volume or compliance
data.maxV = volumefunc(Ar0,data)*VCon;
data.maxdisp = dispfunc(Ar0,data)*CCon;
% Initial compliance and volume
[initial disp] = dispfunc(Ar0,data);
[initial volume] = volumefunc(Ar0,data);
% Optimal area statically determinant structure
[comp] = trussGrowth(data);
comp opt e = data.maxdisp/ne;
Ar opt = (comp/comp opt e).*Ar0;
% Boundary of areas
lb = zeros(size(Ar0,1),1);
ub = zeros(size(Ar0,1),1);
lb(:,1) = Amin;
ub(:,1) = Amax;
% Topology optimization
options = optimset('Algorithm','interiorŌłÆpoint','FinDiffType','central'...
,'GradObj','on','GradConstr','on','DerivativeCheck','off','Display'...
,'iterŌłÆdetailed','Maxiter',400,'MaxFunEvals',15000,'TolX',1eŌłÆ10,...
'TolCon',5eŌłÆ10,'TolFun',1eŌłÆ10);

[ Ar,FVAL,EXITFLAG,OUTPUT ] = fmincon(@(Ar) dispfunc(Ar,data),Ar0,...
[],[],[],[],lb,ub,@(Ar) volumecon(Ar,data),options);
elseif Opt == 2

[],[],[],[],lb,ub,@(Ar) dispcon(Ar,data),options);
end

truss

disp = dispfunc(Ar,data)
vol = volumefunc(Ar,data)

dispfunc.m
function [ disp, graddisp ] = dispfunc(IN,data)
% Function calculates displacement (Xg) or compliance (Ar) of truss structure
% Modified 14/03ŌłÆ2014 by MJB
% Modified 24/08ŌłÆ2014 by LMC
% IN is either Xg or Ar
% Loading data
X=data.X;IX=data.IX;mprop=data.mprop;loads=data.loads;bound=data.bound;
Popt=data.Popt;
% Initializing
neqn = size(X,1)*size(X,2);
% Number of equations
ne = size(IX,1);
% Number of elements
% Vectorization of stiffness matrix
ik = zeros(4*ne,1);
jk = zeros(4*ne,1);
xk = zeros(4*ne,1);
cc = 1;
P=zeros(neqn,1);
% Force vector
D=zeros(neqn,1);
% Displacement vector
disp = 0;
% Compliance
Xorg = X;
if size(IN,1)/2 < size(X,1) && size(IN,1) ╦£= size(IX,1)
graddisp = zeros(neqn,1);
% Gradient vector
else
graddisp = zeros(ne,1);
% Gradient vector
end
% Reestablish X from Xg if IN = Xg
if size(IN,1)/2 < size(X,1) && size(IN,1) ╦£= size(IX,1)
j = 1;
nremove = [ bound(:,1) ; loads(:,1) ];
nremove = unique(nremove);
nremove = sort(nremove);
for i = 1:size(Xorg,1)
if i ╦£= nremove(:)
X(i,1) = IN(j);
X(i,2) = IN(j+1);
j = j+2;
end
end
end
% Stiffness matrix K
for e = 1:ne
node1 = IX(e,1);
node2 = IX(e,2);
dof1=IX(e,1)*2ŌłÆ1;
%x1
dof2=IX(e,1)*2;
%y1
dof3=IX(e,2)*2ŌłÆ1;
%x2
dof4=IX(e,2)*2;
%y2
edof = [ dof1 dof2 dof3 dof4 ];
dX = (X(node2,1)ŌłÆX(node1,1));
dY = (X(node2,2)ŌłÆX(node1,2));
23
==PAGE:120==
H.2. DISPFUNC.M
APPENDIX H. CODE
E = mprop(IX(e,3),1);
if size(IN,1)/2 < size(Xorg,1) && size(IN,1) ╦£= size(IX,1)
A = mprop(IX(e,3),2);
else
A = IN(e);
end
L0 = sqrt(dX╦å2+dY╦å2);
B0 = 1/L0╦å2*[ŌłÆdX ŌłÆdY dX dY ]';
ke = A*E*L0*B0*B0';
for i = 1:4
for j = 1:4
ik(cc) = edof(i);
jk(cc) = edof(j);
xk(cc) = ke(i,j);
cc = cc+1;
end
end
end
K = sparse(ik,jk,xk);
% Force vector
for p = 1:size(loads,1)
P(loads(p,1)*2+loads(p,2)ŌłÆ2,1) = loads(p,3);
end
% BC ŌłÆCorrected stiffness matrix K
Nvec = ones(neqn,1);
for b = 1:size(bound,1)
Nvec(bound(b,1)*2+bound(b,2)ŌłÆ2) = 0;
end
N = sparse(diag(Nvec));
K = N'*K*N +
(eye(size(N))ŌłÆN);
% Displacements
D = K\P;
% if is for IN = Xg /displacement, else is for IN = Ar /compliance
if size(IN,1)/2 < size(X,1) && size(IN,1) ╦£= size(IX,1)
% One load only system
if loads(1,2) == 1
i = 1;
elseif loads(1,2) == 2
i = 0;
end
if loads(1,3) > 0
disp = D(loads(1,1)*2ŌłÆi);
else
disp = ŌłÆD(loads(1,1)*2ŌłÆi);
end
% Gradients
if nargout > 1 % Gradient required
for e = 1:ne
node1 = IX(e,1);
node2 = IX(e,2);
dof1=IX(e,1)*2ŌłÆ1;
%x1
dof2=IX(e,1)*2;
%y1
dof3=IX(e,2)*2ŌłÆ1;
%x2
dof4=IX(e,2)*2;
%y2
24
==PAGE:121==
H.2. DISPFUNC.M
APPENDIX H. CODE
edof = [ dof1 dof2 dof3 dof4 ];
dX = (X(node2,1)ŌłÆX(node1,1));
dY = (X(node2,2)ŌłÆX(node1,2));
E = mprop(IX(e,3),1);
A = mprop(IX(e,3),2);
L0 = sqrt(dX╦å2+dY╦å2);
B0 = 1/L0*[ ŌłÆdX ŌłÆdY dX dY ];
ee = 1/L0*[ X(node2,1)ŌłÆX(node1,1)
X(node2,2)ŌłÆX(node1,2) ];
% Initializing system
u = zeros(1,4);
h1=ŌłÆE*A/L0╦å2*ee;
h2=1/L0*(eye(2)ŌłÆee*ee');
d = D(edof);
for j = 1:4
if j == 1
h = [ ŌłÆ1 0 ];
elseif j == 2
h = [ 0 ŌłÆ1 ];
elseif j == 3
h = [ 1 0 ];
elseif j == 4
h = [ 0 1 ];
end
% Derivative of De
dD = h*h1;
% Derivative of ee
dee = h2*h';
% Derivative of B0
dB0 = [ ŌłÆdee' dee' ];
% Derivative of Ke
dke = 2*dB0'*E*A/L0*B0 + B0'*dD*B0;
u(j) = ŌłÆd'*dke*d;
end
graddisp(edof,1) = graddisp(edof,1) + u';
end
% Assembling gradients
graddisp([2*nremoveŌłÆ1;2*nremove],:) = [];
if Popt == 1
[ stop ] = PlotX(IN,data); % Plot structure during optimization
end
end
else
% Compliance
for e=1:ne
node1 = IX(e,1);
node2 = IX(e,2);
dof1 = IX(e,1)*2ŌłÆ1;
%x1
dof2 = IX(e,1)*2;
%y1
dof3 = IX(e,2)*2ŌłÆ1;
%x2
dof4 = IX(e,2)*2;
%y2
edof = [ dof1 dof2 dof3 dof4 ];

dX = (X(node2,1)ŌłÆX(node1,1));
dY = (X(node2,2)ŌłÆX(node1,2));
E = mprop(IX(e,3),1);

H.3. VOLUMEFUNC.M

volumefunc.m
function [ V, gradV ] = volumefunc(IN,data)
%Function calculates volumen of truss structure
% Modified 10/03ŌłÆ2014 by MJB
%IN is either Xg or Ar
%Loading data
X=data.X;IX=data.IX;mprop=data.mprop;loads=data.loads;bound=data.bound;Popt=data.Popt;
ne = size(IX,1);
% Number of elements
gradients = zeros(size(X,1),2);
% Full gradient vector
gradV = zeros(size(IN,1),1);
% Output gradient vector
V = 0;
% Volumen of truss structure
Xorg = X;
%Reestablish X from Xg if IN = Xg
if size(IN,1)/2 < size(X,1) && size(IN,1) ╦£= size(IX,1)
j = 1;
nremove = [ bound(:,1) ; loads(:,1) ];
nremove = unique(nremove);
nremove = sort(nremove);
for i = 1:size(Xorg,1)
if i ╦£= nremove(:)
X(i,1) = IN(j);
X(i,2) = IN(j+1);
j = j+2;
end
end
end
% Volume of truss
for e = 1:ne
node1 = IX(e,1);
node2 = IX(e,2);
dX = (X(node2,1)ŌłÆX(node1,1));
dY = (X(node2,2)ŌłÆX(node1,2));
if size(IN,1)/2 < size(Xorg,1) && size(IN,1) ╦£= size(IX,1)
A = mprop(IX(e,3),2);
else
A = IN(e);
end
L0 = sqrt(dX╦å2+dY╦å2);
V = V + A*L0;
if nargout > 1 % gradient required
if size(IN,1)/2 < size(Xorg,1) && size(IN,1) ╦£= size(IX,1)
h11 = [ ŌłÆ1 0 ];
h12 = [ 0 ŌłÆ1 ];
h21 = [ 1 0 ];
h22 = [ 0 1 ];
ee = A/L0*[ X(node2,1)ŌłÆX(node1,1)
X(node2,2)ŌłÆX(node1,2) ];
gradients(node1,1) = gradients(node1,1) + h11*ee;
gradients(node1,2) = gradients(node1,2) + h12*ee;
27
==PAGE:124==
H.3. VOLUMEFUNC.M
APPENDIX H. CODE
gradients(node2,1) = gradients(node2,1) + h21*ee;
gradients(node2,2) = gradients(node2,2) + h22*ee;
else
gradV(e) = L0;
end
end
end
if nargout > 1
if size(IN,1)/2 < size(Xorg,1) && size(IN,1) ╦£= size(IX,1)
%Assembling gradients into gradV
gradients(nremove,:) = [];
for i=1:size(gradients,1)
gradV(2*iŌłÆ1,1) = gradients(i,1); %dof1 coordinate
gradV(2*i,1) = gradients(i,2);
%dof2 coordinate
end
end
if Popt == 1
[ stop ] = PlotX(IN,data);
end
end
end

function [ c, ceq, gradc, gradceq ] = volumecon(IN,data)
% Constraint on volume, when compliance is optimized
% Modified 10/03ŌłÆ2014 by MJB
% Modified 25/08ŌłÆ2015 by LMC
%IN is either Xg or Ar
% Loading data
maxV=data.maxV;
if nargout > 2
[ V , gradV ] = volumefunc(IN,data);
gradc = gradV/maxV; % Gradiant is normalized
gradceq = zeros(size(IN,1),1);
else
[ V ] = volumefunc(IN,data);
end
c = V/maxVŌłÆ1;
ceq = 0;
end

dispcon.m
function [ c, ceq, gradc, gradceq ] = dispcon(IN,data)
% Constraint on displacement, when volume is optimized
% Modified 14/03ŌłÆ2014 by MJB
% Modified 25/08ŌłÆ2015 by LMC
%Loading data
maxdisp=data.maxdisp;loads=data.loads;
if nargout > 2
[ disp, graddisp ] = dispfunc(IN,data);
gradc = graddisp/maxdisp; % Gradiant is normalized
gradceq = zeros(size(IN,1),1);
else
[ disp ] = dispfunc(IN,data);
end
% One load only system
if loads(1,3) >= 0
c = ŌłÆ(disp/maxdispŌłÆ1);
else
c = (disp/maxdispŌłÆ1);
end
ceq = 0;
end

truss.m
% Basis truss program
% Modified 3/9ŌłÆ106 by OS
% Modified 20/8ŌłÆ2012 by JSJ
% Modified 14/03ŌłÆ2014 by MJB
% Modified 25/08ŌłÆ2015 by LMC
neqn = size(X,1)*size(X,2);
% Number of equations
ne = size(IX,1);
% Number of elements
% Initialize Global Variables
% Vectorization of stiffness matrix
ik = zeros(4*ne,1);
jk = zeros(4*ne,1);
xk = zeros(4*ne,1);
cc = 1;
P=zeros(neqn,1);
% Force vector
D=zeros(neqn,1);
% Displacement vector
R=zeros(neqn,1);
% Residual vector
strain=zeros(ne,1);
% Element strain vector
strain N=zeros(ne,1);
% Element strain vector
stress=zeros(ne,1);
% Element stress vector
N=zeros(ne,1);
% Element normal force vector
% Stiffness matrix K
for e = 1:ne
node1 = IX(e,1);
node2 = IX(e,2);
dof1=IX(e,1)*2ŌłÆ1;
%x1
dof2=IX(e,1)*2;
%y1
dof3=IX(e,2)*2ŌłÆ1;
%x2
dof4=IX(e,2)*2;
%y2
edof = [ dof1 dof2 dof3 dof4 ];
dX = (X(node2,1)ŌłÆX(node1,1));
dY = (X(node2,2)ŌłÆX(node1,2));
E = mprop(IX(e,3),1);
if exist('Ar','var') == 1
A = Ar(e);
else
A = mprop(IX(e,3),2);
end
L0 = sqrt(dX╦å2+dY╦å2);
B0 = 1/L0╦å2*[ŌłÆdX ŌłÆdY dX dY ]';
ke = A*E*L0*B0*B0';
for i = 1:4
for j = 1:4
ik(cc) = edof(i);
jk(cc) = edof(j);
xk(cc) = ke(i,j);
cc = cc+1;
end
end
end
K = sparse(ik,jk,xk);

function [ stress ] = stressfunc(Ar,data)
%Loading data
X=data.X;IX=data.IX;mprop=data.mprop;loads=data.loads;bound=data.bound;

D=zeros(neqn,1);

node2 = IX(e,2);
dof1=IX(e,1)*2ŌłÆ1;
% x1
dof2=IX(e,1)*2;
% y1
dof3=IX(e,2)*2ŌłÆ1;
% x2
dof4=IX(e,2)*2;
% y2
edof = [ dof1 dof2 dof3 dof4 ];
dX = (X(node2,1)ŌłÆX(node1,1));
dY = (X(node2,2)ŌłÆX(node1,2));
E = mprop(IX(e,3),1);
A = Ar(e);
L0 = sqrt(dX╦å2+dY╦å2);
B0 = 1/L0╦å2*[ŌłÆdX ŌłÆdY dX dY ]';

H.9. GEOMOPT.M
APPENDIX H. CODE
H.9
GeomOpt.m
% Basic truss geometry optimization program
% Modified 14/03ŌłÆ2014 by MJB
% Modified 25/08ŌłÆ2015 by LMC
clc; clear all; close all; format shortg
addpath('Input')
% Loading input file
% testfile
% testfile2
Cantilever
% Choose what to optimize ( 1 = volume, 2 = displacement)
Gopt = 1;
% Choose to use gradients (1 = no, 2 = yes)
opt gradient = 2;
% Chose to plot structure during optimization (1 = yes, 0 = no)
Popt = 0;
% Additional options
dispCon = 1.4;
% Percent change of initial displacement when constrained
VCon = 1.1;
% Percent change of initial volume when constrained
% Saving input in data
data.X=X;data.IX=IX;data.mprop=mprop;data.loads=loads;data.bound=bound;...
data.Popt=Popt;data.lwmax=0;
IXorg = IX;
% Nodes to be optimized
% Xg is the vector to be optimized Xg = [ x1 y1 x2 y2 x3 y3 ... ]
nremove = [ bound(:,1) ; loads(:,1) ]; % Removing boundary and load nodes
nremove = unique(nremove);
nremove = sort(nremove);
Xtemp = X; Xorg = X;
Xtemp(nremove,:) = [];
Xg0 = zeros(size(Xtemp,1)*2,1);
for i=1:size(Xtemp,1)
Xg0(2*iŌłÆ1,1) = Xtemp(i,1); % dof1 coordinate
Xg0(2*i,1) = Xtemp(i,2);
% dof2 coordinate
end
% Constraints
data.maxdisp = dispfunc(Xg0,data)*dispCon;
data.maxV = volumefunc(Xg0,data)*VCon;
% Initial values
initial dips = dispfunc(Xg0,data);
initial vol = volumefunc(Xg0,data);
% Boundary of domain (rectangle)
boundx = 20;
Dbound = [ min(X(:,1))ŌłÆboundx max(X(:,1))+boundx min(X(:,2))ŌłÆboundx...
max(X(:,2)+boundx) ];
% Restriction on domain of each node
% [ lb, ub ] = localboundaries(X,Xg0,Dbound)
lb = zeros(size(Xg0,1),1);
ub = zeros(size(Xg0,1),1);

==PAGE:135==
H.9. GEOMOPT.M
APPENDIX H. CODE
for i=1:size(Xg0)
if mod(i,2) ╦£= 0 % Odd number ŌłÆxŌłÆcoordinate
lb(i,1) = Dbound(1,1);
ub(i,1) = Dbound(1,2);
else
% Even number ŌłÆyŌłÆcoordinate
lb(i,1) = Dbound(1,3);
ub(i,1) = Dbound(1,4);
end
end
% Geometry optimization
if opt gradient == 1
options = optimset('Algorithm','interiorŌłÆpoint','FinDiffType',...
'central','GradObj','off','GradConstr','off','DerivativeCheck',...
'on','Display','iterŌłÆdetailed','Maxiter',400,'MaxFunEvals',...
15000,'TolX',5eŌłÆ6,'TolCon',5eŌłÆ6,'TolFun',1eŌłÆ6);
elseif opt gradient == 2
options = optimset('Algorithm','interiorŌłÆpoint','FinDiffType',...
'central','GradObj','on','GradConstr','on','DerivativeCheck',...
'off','Display','iterŌłÆdetailed','Maxiter',600,'TolX',5eŌłÆ6,...
'TolCon',5eŌłÆ6,'TolFun',1eŌłÆ6);
end

% Optimization of volume with displacement as constraint

[],[],[],[],lb,ub,@(Xg) dispcon(Xg,data),options);
elseif Gopt == 2
% Optimization of displacement with volume as constraint
[ Xg,FVAL,EXITFLAG,OUTPUT ] = fmincon(@(Xg) dispfunc(Xg,data),Xg0,...
[],[],[],[],lb,ub,@(Xg) volumecon(Xg,data),options);
end

j = 1;
for i = 1:size(Xorg,1)
if i ╦£= nremove(:)
X(i,1) = Xg(j);
X(i,2) = Xg(j+1);
j = j+2;
end
end

truss
% Final displacement and volume
disp = dispfunc(Xg,data)
vol = volumefunc(Xg,data)

TGOpt.m
% Truss optimization program
% Modified 12/05ŌłÆ2014 by MJB
% Modified 10/12ŌłÆ2015 by LMC

addpath('Input')
addpath('Plotting')
% Loading input file

Cantilever

function [ disp, graddisp ] = TGfunc(ArXg,IX,X,data)
%Function calculates objective
% Modified 12/05ŌłÆ2014 by MJB
% Modified 15/08ŌłÆ2015 by LMC
% Loading data
% global FE con sens con
% X=data.X;IX=data.IX;

mult ex=data.mult ex; % nremove=data.nremove;
if mult ex == 1
mult = data.mult;
cases = data.cases;
end
% Initializing
ne = size(IX,1);
% Number of elements
neqn = size(X,1)*size(X,2);
% Number of equations
% Vectorization of stiffness matrix
ik = zeros(16*ne,1);
jk = zeros(16*ne,1);
xk = zeros(16*ne,1);
cc = 1;
if mult ex == 1
P=zeros(neqn,cases);
% Force vector

% Displacement vector
else
P=zeros(neqn,1);
% Force vector
D=zeros(neqn,1);
% Displacement vector
end

disp = zeros(1,cases);
% Compliance
else
disp = 0;
% Compliance
end

if mult ex == 1
graddispAr = zeros(ne,cases);
% Gradient vector for areas
graddispXg = zeros(neqn,cases);
% Gradient vector for nodes
else
graddispAr = zeros(ne,1);
% Gradient vector for areas
graddispXg = zeros(neqn,1);
% Gradient vector for nodes
end
Ar = ArXg(1:ne,1);
Xg = ArXg(size(Ar,1)+1:size(ArXg,1),1);
% Reestablish X from Xg
if size(Xg,1) == 0
| |
size(Xg,1) > 2
j = 1;
nremove = [ bound(:,1) ; loads(:,1) ];

function [ V, gradV ] = TGvolumefunc(ArXg,IX,X,data)
%Function calculates volumen of truss structure
% Modified 10/03ŌłÆ2014 by MJB
% Modified 15/08ŌłÆ2015 by LMC
% Loading data
% global sens obj
% X=data.X;IX=data.IX;

L = data.L;
h = data.h;
centrum = data.centrum;
radius = data.radius;
geo penal = data.geo penal;
end
if init == 0
volint = 1;
elseif init == 1
volint = data.volint;
end
% Initializing
ne = size(IX,1);
% Number of elements
V = 0;

| |
size(Xg,1) > 2
j = 1;

nremove = sort(nremove);

end
end

X(size(X,1),1) = Xg(1);

for e = 1:ne

gradients(node2,2) = gradients(node2,2) + h22*ee*A;

gradients(node1,1) = gradients(node1,1) + h11*ee*Ar(e)...
+ geo penal*(double(dcdx1(x1,y1,x2,y2))...
*L0+double(cross length(x1,y1,x2,y2))*h11*ee);
gradients(node1,2) = gradients(node1,2) + h12*ee*Ar(e)...
+ geo penal*(double(dcdy1(x1,y1,x2,y2))...
*L0+double(cross length(x1,y1,x2,y2))*h12*ee);
gradients(node2,1) = gradients(node2,1) + h21*ee*Ar(e)...
+ geo penal*(double(dcdx2(x1,y1,x2,y2))...
*L0+double(cross length(x1,y1,x2,y2))*h21*ee);
gradients(node2,2) = gradients(node2,2) + h22*ee*Ar(e)...
+ geo penal*(double(dcdy2(x1,y1,x2,y2))...
*L0+double(cross length(x1,y1,x2,y2))*h22*ee);
end
gradVAr(e) = L0;
end
end
% Normalize volume
V = V/volint;
if nargout > 1
% Assembling gradients into gradV
gradients(nremove,:) = [];
for i=1:size(gradients,1)
gradVXg(2*iŌłÆ1,1) = gradients(i,1); % dof1 coordinate
gradVXg(2*i,1) = gradients(i,2);
% dof2 coordinate
end
gradV = [ gradVAr
gradVXg ];
gradV = gradV/volint;
%
sens obj = sens obj + 1;
end
end

function [ c, ceq, gradc, gradceq ] = TGcondisp(ArXg,IX,X,data)

else
[ disp ] = TGfunc(ArXg,IX,X,data);
end
c = disp/maxcompŌłÆ1;

end

H.22. LOCALBOUNDARIES.M
APPENDIX H. CODE
H.22
localboundaries.m
function [ lbXg, ubXg ] = localboundaries(X,Xg0,Dbound)
% Function finds local boundaries for free nodes
% Modified 13/05ŌłÆ2014 by MJB
% Modified 25/08ŌłÆ2014 by LMC
% Additional reduction of local boundaries
lmin = 0.9;
% Initializing
lbXg = zeros(size(Xg0,1),1);
lbXg(:) = 1e20;
ubXg = zeros(size(Xg0,1),1);
ubXg(:) = 1e20;
% Local boundaries for all free nodes
for i=1:2:size(Xg0) % every pair of nodes
j = 0;
% Node is found and ignored in system
xnode = [ Xg0(i,1) Xg0(i+1,1) ];
Xtemp2 = X;
[╦£,indx] = ismember(xnode,X,'rows');
Xtemp2(indx,:) = [];
nel = size(Xtemp2,1);
% Neighboring nodes defines boundaries
while ( ismember(1e20,lbXg) == 1
| |
ismember(1e20,ubXg) == 1 ) ...
&& j < nel
IDX = knnsearch(Xtemp2,xnode); % Closest node
% Nearest node is in NW
if Xtemp2(IDX,1) <= xnode(1,1) && Xtemp2(IDX,2) >= xnode(1,2)
if ( abs(xnode(1,1)ŌłÆXtemp2(IDX,1)) < abs(xnode(1,2)ŌłÆ...
Xtemp2(IDX,2)) ) && ubXg(i+1,1)
== 1e20
ubXg(i+1,1) = (xnode(1,2)+Xtemp2(IDX,2))/2;
elseif ( abs(xnode(1,1)ŌłÆXtemp2(IDX,1)) >= abs(xnode(1,2)...
ŌłÆXtemp2(IDX,2)) ) && lbXg(i,1) == 1e20
lbXg(i,1) = (xnode(1,1)+Xtemp2(IDX,1))/2;
end
% Nearest node is in NE
elseif Xtemp2(IDX,1) > xnode(1,1) && Xtemp2(IDX,2) >= xnode(1,2)
if ( abs(xnode(1,1)ŌłÆXtemp2(IDX,1)) < abs(xnode(1,2)...
ŌłÆXtemp2(IDX,2)) ) && ubXg(i+1,1)
== 1e20
ubXg(i+1,1) = (xnode(1,2)+Xtemp2(IDX,2))/2;
elseif ( abs(xnode(1,1)ŌłÆXtemp2(IDX,1)) >= abs(xnode(1,2)...
ŌłÆXtemp2(IDX,2)) ) && ubXg(i,1) == 1e20
ubXg(i,1) = (xnode(1,1)+Xtemp2(IDX,1))/2;
end
% Nearest node is in SW
elseif Xtemp2(IDX,1) <= xnode(1,1) && Xtemp2(IDX,2) < xnode(1,2)
if ( abs(xnode(1,1)ŌłÆXtemp2(IDX,1)) < abs(xnode(1,2)...
ŌłÆXtemp2(IDX,2)) ) && lbXg(i+1,1) == 1e20
lbXg(i+1,1) = (xnode(1,2)+Xtemp2(IDX,2))/2;
elseif ( abs(xnode(1,1)ŌłÆXtemp2(IDX,1)) >= abs(xnode(1,2)...
ŌłÆXtemp2(IDX,2)) ) && lbXg(i,1) == 1e20
lbXg(i,1) = (xnode(1,1)+Xtemp2(IDX,1))/2;
end
77
==PAGE:174==
H.22. LOCALBOUNDARIES.M
APPENDIX H. CODE
% Nearest node is in SE
elseif Xtemp2(IDX,1) > xnode(1,1) && Xtemp2(IDX,2) < xnode(1,2)
if ( abs(xnode(1,1)ŌłÆXtemp2(IDX,1)) < abs(xnode(1,2)...
ŌłÆXtemp2(IDX,2)) ) && lbXg(i+1,1) == 1e20
lbXg(i+1,1) = (xnode(1,2)+Xtemp2(IDX,2))/2;
elseif
( abs(xnode(1,1)ŌłÆXtemp2(IDX,1)) >= abs(xnode(1,2)...
ŌłÆXtemp2(IDX,2)) ) && ubXg(i,1) == 1e20
ubXg(i,1) = (xnode(1,1)+Xtemp2(IDX,1))/2;
end
end
j = j+1;
% The present nearest node is ignored in next check
Xtemp2(IDX,:) = [];
end
% If no neighboring nodes, the global boundaries are used
if lbXg(i,1) == 1e20
lbXg(i,1) = Dbound(1,1);
end
if ubXg(i,1) == 1e20
ubXg(i,1) = Dbound(1,2);
end
if lbXg(i+1,1) == 1e20
lbXg(i+1,1) = Dbound(1,3);
end
if ubXg(i+1,1) == 1e20
ubXg(i+1,1) = Dbound(1,4);
end
end
% Reduction of boundaries
lbXg = lbXg+((Xg0ŌłÆlbXg)*(1ŌłÆlmin));
ubXg = ubXgŌłÆ((ubXgŌłÆXg0)*(1ŌłÆlmin));
end

H.23. COMPCHECK.M

compcheck.m
function [ disp, Ar, IX ] = compcheck(ArXg,IX,X,data)
% Function calculates compliance after element removal
% Modified 15/08ŌłÆ2015 by LMC
% Loading data
mprop=data.mprop;loads=data.loads;bound=data.bound;Popt=data.Popt;
mult ex=data.mult ex;remove factor=data.remove factor;
if mult ex == 1
mult = data.mult;
cases = data.cases;
end
% Initializing
ne = size(IX,1);
% Number of elements
neqn = size(X,1)*size(X,2);
% Number of equations
if mult ex == 1
P=zeros(neqn,cases);
% Force vector
D=zeros(neqn,cases);
% Displacement vector
else
P=zeros(neqn,1);
% Force vector
D=zeros(neqn,1);
% Displacement vector
end
if mult ex == 1
disp = zeros(1,cases);
% Compliance
else
disp = 0;
% Compliance
end
Xorg = X;
Ar = ArXg(1:ne,1);
Xg = ArXg(size(Ar,1)+1:size(ArXg,1),1);
% Remove small members
nremove = [];
i = 1;
for ee=1:size(IX,1)
if Ar(ee) < remove factor*max(Ar);
nremove(i) = ee;
i = i + 1;
end
end
nremove = sort(nremove);
Ar(nremove,:) = [];
IX(nremove,:) = [];
ne = size(IX,1);
ik = zeros(16*ne,1);
jk = zeros(16*ne,1);
xk = zeros(16*ne,1);
cc = 1;
nremove = [];
%Reestablish X from Xg
if size(Xg,1) == 0
| |
size(Xg,1) > 2
j = 1;
nremove = [ bound(:,1) ; loads(:,1) ];
nremove = unique(nremove);

node2 = IX(e,2);

% x2

dY = (X(node2,2)ŌłÆX(node1,2));

B0 = [ŌłÆdX/L0╦å2 ŌłÆdY/L0╦å2 dX/L0╦å2 dY/L0╦å2 ]';
ke(:,:,e) = A*E*L0*(B0*B0');
for i = 1:4
for j = 1:4
ik(cc) = edof(i);
jk(cc) = edof(j);
xk(cc) = ke(i,j,e);
cc = cc+1;
end
end
end
K = sparse(ik,jk,xk);

if mult ex == 1
ppp =
0;

for p = 1:mult
P(loads(p+ppp,1)*2+loads(p+ppp,2)ŌłÆ2,pp) = loads(p+ppp,3);
end
ppp = ppp+mult;
end
else
for p = 1:size(loads,1)
P(loads(p,1)*2+loads(p,2)ŌłÆ2,1) = loads(p,3);
end
end

% BC ŌłÆCorrected stiffness matrix K
Nvec = ones(neqn,1);
for b = 1:size(bound,1)
Nvec(bound(b,1)*2+bound(b,2)ŌłÆ2) = 0;
end

K = N'*K*N +
(eye(size(N))ŌłÆN);

else

% x1
dof2 = IX(e,1)*2;
% y1
dof3 = IX(e,2)*2ŌłÆ1;
% x2
dof4 = IX(e,2)*2;
% y2
edof = [ dof1 dof2 dof3 dof4 ];
A = Ar(e);
d=D(edof,:);
for i=1:cases
disp(1,i) = disp(1,i) + d(:,i)'*ke(:,:,e)*d(:,i);
end
end
end
else
% Compliances
if mult ex == 1
for i=1:cases
disp(1,i) = 1e10;
end
else
disp = 1e10;
end
end
if Popt == 1
[ stop ] = PlotX(ArXg,data);
end

function [ disp, graddisp ] = dispfunc3D(IN,data)
% Function calculates displacement (Xg) or compliance (Ar)
% Modified 20/09ŌłÆ2015 by LMC
% IN is either Xg or Ar
% Loading data
X=data.X;IX=data.IX;mprop=data.mprop;loads=data.loads;bound=data.bound;
Popt=data.Popt;mult ex=data.mult ex;fake supp=data.fake supp;
fake supp fac=data.fake supp fac;
if mult ex == 1
mult = data.mult;
cases = data.cases;
end

% Number of equations
ne = size(IX,1);
% Number of elements

jk = zeros(6*ne,1);
xk = zeros(6*ne,1);

P=zeros(neqn,cases);
% Force vector
D=zeros(neqn,cases);
% Displacement vector
else
P=zeros(neqn,1);
% Force vector
D=zeros(neqn,1);
% Displacement vector
end

disp = zeros(1,cases);
% Compliance
else
disp = 0;
% Compliance
end
Xorg = X;
if size(IN,1)/3 < size(X,1) && size(IN,1) ╦£= size(IX,1)

% Gradient vector
else
graddisp = zeros(ne,1);
% Gradient vector
end

j = 1;

nremove = unique(nremove);

function [ V, gradV ] = volumefunc3D(IN,data)
% Function calculates volume of truss structure
% Modified 20/09ŌłÆ2015 by LMC
% IN is either Xg or Ar
% Loading data
X=data.X;IX=data.IX;mprop=data.mprop;loads=data.loads;bound=data.bound;Popt=data.Popt;
ne = size(IX,1);
% Number of elements
gradients = zeros(size(X,1),3);
% Full gradient vector
gradV = zeros(size(IN,1),1);
% Output gradient vector
V = 0;
% Volumen of truss structure
Xorg = X;
% Reestablish X from Xg if IN = Xg
if size(IN,1)/3 < size(X,1) && size(IN,1) ╦£= size(IX,1)
j = 1;
nremove = [ bound(:,1) ; loads(:,1) ];
nremove = unique(nremove);
nremove = sort(nremove);
for i = 1:size(Xorg,1)
if i ╦£= nremove(:)
X(i,1) = IN(j);
X(i,2) = IN(j+1);
X(i,3) = IN(j+2);
j = j+3;
end
end
end
% Volume of truss
for e = 1:ne
node1 = IX(e,1);
node2 = IX(e,2);
dX = (X(node2,1)ŌłÆX(node1,1));
dY = (X(node2,2)ŌłÆX(node1,2));
dZ = (X(node2,3)ŌłÆX(node1,3));
if size(IN,1)/3 < size(Xorg,1) && size(IN,1) ╦£= size(IX,1)
A = mprop(IX(e,3),2);
else
A = IN(e);
end
L0 = sqrt(dX╦å2+dY╦å2+dZ╦å2);
V = V + A*L0;
if nargout > 1 % gradient required
if size(IN,1)/3 < size(Xorg,1) && size(IN,1) ╦£= size(IX,1)
h11 = [ ŌłÆ1 0 0 ];
h12 = [ 0 ŌłÆ1 0 ];
h13 = [ 0 0 ŌłÆ1 ];

h23 = [ 0 0 1

gradients(node1,2) = gradients(node1,2) + h12*ee;

function [ c, ceq, gradc, gradceq ] = volumecon3D(IN,data)
% Constraint on volume, when displacement is optimized

% IN is either Xg or Ar
% Loading data

[ V , gradV ] = volumefunc3D(IN,data);

gradceq = zeros(size(IN,1),1);
else
[ V ] = volumefunc3D(IN,data);
end
c = V/maxVŌłÆ1;
ceq = 0;

% Basic 3D truss shape optimization program
% Modified 20/09ŌłÆ2015 by LMC
clc; clear all; close all; format shortg
addpath('Input3D')
% Loading input file
% testfile2 3D
box cantilever 3D
% bridge3D
data.mult ex = 0;
data.fake supp = 2;
data.fake supp fac = 1eŌłÆ8;
% Choose what to optimize ( 1 = volume, 2 = displacement)
Gopt = 1;
% Choose to use gradients (1 = no, 2 = yes)
opt gradient = 2;
% Choose to plot structure during optimization (1 = yes, 2 = no)
Popt = 2;
% Additional options
dispCon = 1.4;
% Percent change of initial displacement when constrained
VCon = 1.1;
% Percent change of initial volume when constrained
% Saving input in data
data.X=X;data.IX=IX;data.mprop=mprop;data.loads=loads;data.bound=bound;data.Popt=Popt;data.lwmax=0;
IXorg = IX;
% Nodes to be optimized
% Xg is the vector to be optimized Xg = [ x1 y1 z1 x2 y2 z2 x3 y3 z3 ... ]

nremove = unique(nremove);
nremove = sort(nremove);
Xtemp = X; Xorg = X;
Xtemp(nremove,:) = [];

Xg0(3*iŌłÆ1,1) = Xtemp(i,2); % dof2 coordinate

function [ V, gradV ] = TGvolumefunc3D(ArXg,IX,X,data)
% Function calculates volume of 3D truss structure
% Modified 20/09ŌłÆ2015 by LMC
% Loading data
loads=data.loads;bound=data.bound;init=data.init;
if init == 0
volint = 1;
elseif init == 1
volint = data.volint;
end
% Initializing
ne = size(IX,1);
% Number of elements
V = 0;
% Volumen of truss structure
Xorg = X;
Ar = ArXg(1:ne,1);
Xg = ArXg(size(Ar,1)+1:size(ArXg,1),1);
gradients = zeros(size(X,1),3);
% Full gradient vector
gradVAr = zeros(ne,1);
% Gradient vector for areas
gradVXg = zeros(size(Xg,1),1);
% Gradient vector for nodes
% Reestablish X from Xg
if size(Xg,1) == 0
| |
size(Xg,1) > 2
j = 1;
nremove = [ bound(:,1) ; loads(:,1) ];
nremove = unique(nremove);
nremove = sort(nremove);
for i = 1:size(Xorg,1)
if i ╦£= nremove(:)
X(i,1) = Xg(j);
X(i,2) = Xg(j+1);
X(i,3) = Xg(j+2);
j = j+3;
end
end
else
nremove(:,1) = ( 1:(size(X,1)ŌłÆ1) );
X(size(X,1),1) = Xg(1);
X(size(X,1),2) = Xg(2);
X(size(X,1),3) = Xg(3);
end
% Volume of truss
for e = 1:ne
node1 = IX(e,1);
node2 = IX(e,2);

dY = (X(node2,2)ŌłÆX(node1,2));
dZ = (X(node2,3)ŌłÆX(node1,3));
A = Ar(e);

TGcondisp3D.m
function [ c, ceq, gradc, gradceq ] = TGcondisp3D(ArXg,IX,X,data)
% Constraint on compliance, when volume is optimized
% Modified 20/09ŌłÆ2015 by LMC
% Loading data
maxcomp=data.maxcomp;mult ex=data.mult ex;Eig=data.Eig;Eigmin=data.Eigmin;
if mult ex == 1
mult = data.mult;
cases = data.cases;
end
if mult ex == 1
if nargout > 2
[ disp, graddisp ] = TGfunc3D(ArXg,IX,X,data);
for i = 1:cases
gradc(1:size(ArXg,1),i) = graddisp(1:size(ArXg,1),i)/maxcomp(i);
end
gradceq = zeros(size(ArXg,1),cases);
if Eig == 1
gradc(:,cases+1) = graddisp(size(ArXg,1)+1:2*size(ArXg,1))/Eigmin;
gradceq(:,cases+1) = zeros(size(ArXg,1),1);
end
else
[ disp ] = TGfunc3D(ArXg,IX,X,data);
end
for i = 1:cases
c(i,1) = disp(1,i)/maxcomp(1,i)ŌłÆ1;
ceq(i,1) = 0;
end
if Eig == 1
c(cases+1,1) = 1ŌłÆdisp(1,cases+1)/Eigmin;
ceq(cases+1,1) = 0;
end
else
if nargout > 2
[ disp, graddisp ] = TGfunc3D(ArXg,IX,X,data);
gradc(:,1) = graddisp(1:size(ArXg,1),1)/maxcomp;
gradceq = zeros(size(ArXg,1),1);
if Eig == 1
gradc(:,2) = graddisp(size(ArXg,1)+1:2*size(ArXg,1))/Eigmin;
gradceq(:,2) = zeros(size(ArXg,1),1);
end
else
[ disp ] = TGfunc3D(ArXg,IX,X,data);
end
c = disp(1,1)/maxcompŌłÆ1;
ceq = 0;
if Eig == 1
c(2,1) = 1ŌłÆdisp(1,2)/Eigmin;
ceq(2,1) = 0;
end
end
end

H.39. DISTBETWEEN2SEGMENT.M
APPENDIX H. CODE
H.39
DistBetween2Segment.m
% Computes the minimum distance between two line segments. Code
% is adapted for Matlab from Dan Sunday's Geometry Algorithms originally
% written in C++
% http://softsurfer.com/Archive/algorithm 0106/algorithm 0106.htm#dist3D Segment to Segment
% Usage: Input the start and end x,y,z coordinates for two line segments.
% p1, p2 are [x,y,z] coordinates of first line segment and p3,p4 are for
% second line segment.
% Output: scalar minimum distance between the two segments.
%
Example:
%
P1 = [0 0 0];
P2 = [1 0 0];
%
P3 = [0 1 0];
P4 = [1 1 0];
%
dist = DistBetween2Segment(P1, P2, P3, P4)
%
dist = 1
%
%
%
function [distance vec connect point e1 point e2] = DistBetween2Segment...
(p1, p2, p3, p4)
u = p1 ŌłÆp2;
v = p3 ŌłÆp4;
w = p2 ŌłÆp4;
a = dot(u,u);
b = dot(u,v);
c = dot(v,v);
d = dot(u,w);
e = dot(v,w);
D = a*c ŌłÆb*b;
sD = D;
tD = D;
SMALL NUM = 0.00000001;
% compute the line parameters of the two closest points
if (D < SMALL NUM)
% the lines are almost parallel
sN = 0.0;
% force using point P0 on segment S1
sD = 1.0;
% to prevent possible division by 0.0 later
tN = e;
tD = c;
else
% get the closest points on the infinite lines
sN = (b*e ŌłÆc*d);
tN = (a*e ŌłÆb*d);
if (sN < 0.0)
% sc < 0 => the s=0 edge is visible
sN = 0.0;
tN = e;
tD = c;
elseif (sN > sD)% sc > 1 => the s=1 edge is visible
sN = sD;
tN = e + b;
tD = c;
end
end
if (tN < 0.0)
% tc < 0 => the t=0 edge is visible
133
==PAGE:230==
H.39. DISTBETWEEN2SEGMENT.M
APPENDIX H. CODE
tN = 0.0;
% recompute sc for this edge
if (ŌłÆd < 0.0)
sN = 0.0;
elseif (ŌłÆd > a)
sN = sD;
else
sN = ŌłÆd;
sD = a;
end
elseif (tN > tD)
% tc > 1 => the t=1 edge is visible
tN = tD;
% recompute sc for this edge
if ((ŌłÆd + b) < 0.0)
sN = 0;
elseif ((ŌłÆd + b) > a)
sN = sD;
else
sN = (ŌłÆd + b);
sD = a;
end
end
% finally do the division to get sc and tc
if(abs(sN) < SMALL NUM)
sc = 0.0;
else
sc = sN / sD;
end
if(abs(tN) < SMALL NUM)
tc = 0.0;
else
tc = tN / tD;
end
% get the difference of the two closest points
dP = w + (sc * u) ŌłÆ(tc * v);
% = S1(sc) ŌłÆS2(tc)
distance = norm(dP);
outV = dP;
vec connect = outV;
% vector connecting the closest points
point e1 = p2+sc*u;
% Closest point on object 1
point e2 = p4+tc*v;
% Closest point on object 2
end

function [ disp, Ar, IX ] = compcheck3D(ArXg,IX,X,data,remove factor)
% Function calculates compliance after element removal
% Modified 20/09ŌłÆ2015 by LMC
% Loading data
mprop=data.mprop;loads=data.loads;bound=data.bound;Popt=data.Popt;
mult ex=data.mult ex;Eig=data.Eig;fake supp=data.fake supp;fake supp fac=data.fake supp fac;
if mult ex == 1
mult = data.mult;
cases = data.cases;
end
% Initializing
ne = size(IX,1);
% Number of elements
neqn = size(X,1)*size(X,2);
% Number of equations
% Vectorization of stiffness matrix
ik = zeros(6*ne,1);
jk = zeros(6*ne,1);
xk = zeros(6*ne,1);
xm = zeros(6*ne,1);
cc = 1;
if mult ex == 1
P=zeros(neqn,cases);
% Force vector
D=zeros(neqn,cases);
% Displacement vector
else
P=zeros(neqn,1);
% Force vector
D=zeros(neqn,1);
% Displacement vector
end
if mult ex == 1
disp = zeros(1,cases);
% Compliance
else
disp = 0;
% Compliance
end
Xorg = X;
Ar = ArXg(1:ne,1);
Xg = ArXg(size(Ar,1)+1:size(ArXg,1),1);
nremove = [];
i = 1;
for ee=1:size(IX,1)
if Ar(ee) < remove factor*max(Ar);
nremove(i) = ee;
i = i + 1;
end
end
nremove = sort(nremove);
Ar(nremove,:) = [];
IX(nremove,:) = [];
ne = size(IX,1);
% Reestablish X from Xg
if size(Xg,1) == 0
| |
size(Xg,1) > 2
j = 1;
nremove = [ bound(:,1) ; loads(:,1) ];
nremove = unique(nremove);
nremove = sort(nremove);

end

X(size(X,1),1) = Xg(1);
X(size(X,1),2) = Xg(2);
X(size(X,1),3) = Xg(3);
end
B0 = [];

% Stiffness matrix K
for e = 1:ne
node1 = IX(e,1);
node2 = IX(e,2);
dof1=IX(e,1)*3ŌłÆ2;
% x1
dof2=IX(e,1)*3ŌłÆ1;
% y1
dof3=IX(e,1)*3;
% z1
dof4=IX(e,2)*3ŌłÆ2;
% x2
dof5=IX(e,2)*3ŌłÆ1;
% y2
dof6=IX(e,2)*3;
% z2
edof = [ dof1 dof2 dof3 dof4 dof5 dof6 ];
dX = (X(node2,1)ŌłÆX(node1,1));
dY = (X(node2,2)ŌłÆX(node1,2));
dZ = (X(node2,3)ŌłÆX(node1,3));
E = mprop(IX(e,3),1);
rho = mprop(IX(e,3),3);
A = Ar(e);
L0 = sqrt(dX╦å2+dY╦å2+dZ╦å2);
% Stiffness matrix and derivative
B0 = 1/L0╦å2*[ŌłÆdX ŌłÆdY ŌłÆdZ dX dY dZ ]';
ke = A*E*L0*(B0*B0');
for i = 1:6
for j = 1:6
ik(cc) = edof(i);
jk(cc) = edof(j);
xk(cc) = ke(i,j);
cc = cc+1;
end
end
end
K = sparse(ik,jk,xk);
% Force vector
if mult ex == 1
ppp =
0;
for pp = 1:cases
for p = 1:mult
P(loads(p+ppp,1)*3+loads(p+ppp,2)ŌłÆ3,pp) = loads(p+ppp,3);
end
ppp = ppp+mult;
end
else

H.42. COMPCHECK3D.M
APPENDIX H. CODE
for p = 1:size(loads,1)
P(loads(p,1)*3+loads(p,2)ŌłÆ3,1) = loads(p,3);
end

% BC ŌłÆCorrected stiffness matrix K
Nvec = ones(neqn,1);
for b = 1:size(bound,1)
Nvec(bound(b,1)*3+bound(b,2)ŌłÆ3) = 0;
end
N = sparse(diag(Nvec));
K = N'*K*N +
(eye(size(N))ŌłÆN);
% Displacements
D = K\P;
% Compliance
if mult ex == 1
disp = (D'*K*D)';
else
disp = D'*K*D;
end
if Popt == 1
[ stop ] = PlotX3D(ArXg,data);
end
end

%%
function V = objective ipopt(x)
loads=data.loads;bound=data.bound;init=data.init;
nremove=data.nremove;
if init == 0
volint = 1;
elseif init == 1
volint = data.volint;
end
% Initializing
ne = size(IX,1);
% Number of elements
V = 0;
% Volumen of truss structure
Xorg = X;
Ar = x(1,1:ne)';
Xg = x(1,ne+1:size(x,2))';
% Reestablish X from Xg
if size(Xg,1) == 0
| |
size(Xg,1) > 2

function disp = constraints ipopt(x)

H.44. MICHELLCANTILEVERCIRC.M
APPENDIX H. CODE
H.44
MichellCantileverCirc.m
% Cantilever with circular ring of supports
% Parameters
radius = 1;
norm factor = 10;
% norm factor = 3.35889; % Long
% norm factor = 1.82196; % Short
% norm factor = 1; % Really short
L = radius*norm factor; % Length
% Bounded nodes
number supp = 20;
Arcl halfcirc = 2*pi*radius*(180/360);
Arcl = 0:Arcl halfcirc/(number supp/2):Arcl halfcirc;
x = cosd(360*Arcl/(2*pi*radius))*radius;
for i = 1:number supp/2+1
y(i) = sqrt(radius╦å2ŌłÆx(i)╦å2);
X(i,:) = [ x(i) y(i) ];
end
for i = 1:number supp/2+1
if i╦£=1 && i╦£=number supp/2+1
X = [ X ; x(i) ŌłÆy(i) ];
end
end
% Loaded node
X(size(X,1)+1,:) = [ L 0 ];
% Element properties: Young's modulus, area
mprop = [ 100 1 ];
% Nodal diplacements: node id, degree of freedom (1ŌłÆx, 2ŌłÆy), displacement
bound = zeros(size(X,1)ŌłÆ1,3);
for i = 1:size(X,1)ŌłÆ1
bound(2*iŌłÆ1:2*i,:) = [ i 1 0 ; i 2 0 ];
end
% Nodal loads: node id, degree of freedom (1ŌłÆx, 2ŌłÆy), load
loads = [ size(X,1) 2 ŌłÆ1 ];
